Along with “Self-Defence of the Maidan”, there were also some "independent" divisions of enforcers (some of them were also referred to as sotnias and even as “Self-Defence” groups), like the security of the Trade Unions Building until 2 January 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-281">[272]</a></sup> Narnia and Vikings from [Kyiv City State Administration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv_City_State_Administration "Kyiv City State Administration"),<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-282">[273]</a></sup> Volodymr Parasyuk's sotnia from Conservatory building,<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-283">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-284">[275]</a></sup> although Andriy Parubiy officially asked such divisions to not term themselves as “Self-Defence” groups.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-285">[276]</a></sup>

[Pravy Sektor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_Sector "Right Sector") coordinates its actions with Self-defence and is formally a 23rd sotnia,<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-286">[277]</a></sup> although already had hundreds of members at the time of registering as a sotnia. Second sotnia (staffed by Svoboda's members) tends to dissociate itself from "sotnias of self-defence of Maidan".<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-287">[278]</a></sup>

Some Russian citizens sympathetic to the opposition joined the protest movement as part of the [Misanthropic Division](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misanthropic_Division "Misanthropic Division"), many of them later becoming Ukrainian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-misanthropic_41-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-misanthropic-41">[39]</a></sup>

## Casualties

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ukrainian_Red_Cross_Society_volunteers_administering_first_aid_to_a_wounded_Euromaidan_protester._Events_of_Jan_19,_2014-5.jpg)

[Ukrainian Red Cross Society](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Red_Cross_Society "Ukrainian Red Cross Society") volunteers administering first aid to a wounded protester, 19 January 2014

Altogether, more than 100 people were killed and 2,500 injured.<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-288">[279]</a></sup> The death toll included 108 protesters and 13 police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-OHCHR_76-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-OHCHR-76">[71]</a></sup> Most of the deaths and injuries were during the [Revolution of Dignity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity "Revolution of Dignity") in February 2014.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

In November 2015, the Office of the Prosecutor of the [International Criminal Court](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Criminal_Court "International Criminal Court") released a legal analysis of the Maidan protests, concluding that: "violence against protesters, including the excessive use of force causing death and serious injury as well as other forms of ill-treatment, was actively promoted or encouraged by the Ukrainian authorities" under Yanukovych.<sup id="cite_ref-OHCHR_76-6"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-OHCHR-76">[71]</a></sup>

By June 2016, 55 people had been charged in relation to the deaths of Maidan protesters, including 29 former members of the Berkut special police, ten _[titushky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titushky "Titushky")_ and ten senior government officials.<sup id="cite_ref-OHCHR_76-7"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-OHCHR-76">[71]</a></sup>

### Press and medics injured by police attacks

A number of attacks by law enforcement agents on members of the media and [medical personnel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_personnel "Medical personnel") have been reported. Some 40 journalists were injured during the staged assault at Bankova Street on 1 December 2013. At least 42 more journalists were victims of police attacks at Hrushevskoho Street on 22 January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-289">[280]</a></sup> On 22 January 2014, Television News Service (TSN) reported that journalists started to remove their identifying uniform (vests and helmets), as they were being targeted, sometimes on purpose, sometimes accidentally.<sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-290">[281]</a></sup> Since 21 November 2013, a total of 136 journalists have been injured.<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-291">[282]</a></sup>

On 21 January 2014, 26 journalists were injured, with at least two badly injured by police stun grenades;<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-292">[283]</a></sup> 2 others were arrested by police.<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-293">[284]</a></sup> On 22 January, a correspondent of Reuters, Vasiliy Fedosenko, was intentionally shot in the head by a marksman with [rubber ammunition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubber_bullet "Rubber bullet") during clashes at Hrushevskoho Street.<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-294">[285]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-295">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-296">[287]</a></sup> Later, a journalist of [Espresso TV](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Espresso_TV "Espresso TV") Dmytro Dvoychenkov was kidnapped, beaten and taken to an unknown location, but later a parliamentarian was informed that he was finally released.<sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-297">[288]</a></sup> On 24 January, President Yanukovych ordered the release of all journalists from custody.<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-298">[289]</a></sup> On 31 January, a video from 22 January 2014 was published that showed policemen in Berkut uniforms intentionally firing at a medic who raised his hands.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-299">[290]</a></sup> On 18 February 2014, American photojournalist Mark Estabrook was injured by Berkut forces, who threw two separate concussion grenades at him just inside the gate at the Hrushevskoho Street barricade, with shrapnel hitting him in the shoulder and lower leg. He continued bleeding all the way to Cologne, Germany for surgery. He was informed upon his arrival in Maidan to stay away from the hospitals in Kyiv to avoid Yanukovych's Berkut police capture (February 2014)<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-300">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-301">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-302">[293]</a></sup>

## Analysis

### Public opinion about Euromaidan

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Euromaidan_19_January_3.jpg)

Maidan protesters in Kyiv, 19 January 2014

According to December 2013 polls (by three different pollsters), between 45% and 50% of Ukrainians supported Euromaidan, while between 42% and 50% opposed it.<sup id="cite_ref-RBpoll491213_303-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBpoll491213-303">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RBsIU301213_304-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBsIU301213-304">[295]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-razumkov_305-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-razumkov-305">[296]</a></sup> The biggest support for the protest was found in Kyiv (about 75%) and [western Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Ukraine "Western Ukraine") (more than 80%).<sup id="cite_ref-RBpoll491213_303-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBpoll491213-303">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FT291213_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-FT291213-306">[297]</a></sup> Among Euromaidan protesters, 55% were from the west of the country, with 24% from central Ukraine and 21% from the east.<sup id="cite_ref-kpdemographicsfeb_307-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kpdemographicsfeb-307">[298]</a></sup>

In a poll taken on 7–8 December, 73% of protesters had committed to continue protesting in Kyiv as long as needed until their demands were fulfilled.<sup id="cite_ref-3011crackdownRtP_5-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-3011crackdownRtP-5">[5]</a></sup> This number had increased to 82% as of 3 February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-kpdemographicsfeb_307-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kpdemographicsfeb-307">[298]</a></sup> Polls also showed that the nation was divided in age: while a majority of young people were pro-EU, older generations (50 and above) more often preferred the [Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Customs_Union_of_Belarus,_Kazakhstan,_and_Russia "Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia").<sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-308">[299]</a></sup> More than 41% of protesters were ready to take part in the seizure of administrative buildings as of February, compared to 13 and 19 per cent during polls on 10 and 20 December 2013. At the same time, more than 50 per cent were ready to take part in the creation of independent military units, compared to 15 and 21 per cent during the past studies, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-kpdemographicsfeb_307-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kpdemographicsfeb-307">[298]</a></sup>

According to a January poll, 45% of Ukrainians supported the protests, and 48% of Ukrainians disapproved of Euromaidan.<sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-309">[300]</a></sup>

In a March poll, 57% of Ukrainians said they supported the Euromaidan protests.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-310">[301]</a></sup>

A study of public opinion in regular and social media found that 74% of Russian speakers in Ukraine supported the Euromaidan movement, and a quarter opposed.<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-311">[302]</a></sup>

### Support for Euromaidan in Ukraine

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Klitschko_Tyahnybok_Yatsenyuk_Dec_8_2013.jpg)

Opposition leaders, 8 December 2013

According to a 4 to 9 December 2013 study<sup id="cite_ref-RBpoll491213_303-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBpoll491213-303">[294]</a></sup> by Research & Branding Group, 49% of all Ukrainians supported Euromaidan and 45% had the opposite opinion. It was mostly supported in Western (84%) and [Central Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Ukraine "Central Ukraine") (66%). A third (33%) of residents of South Ukraine and 13% of residents of Eastern Ukraine supported Euromaidan as well. The percentage of people who do not support the protesters was 81% in [East Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Ukraine "East Ukraine"), 60% in [South Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ukraine "South Ukraine")<sup id="cite_ref-313"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-313">[nb 10]</a></sup>, in [Central Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Ukraine "Central Ukraine") 27% and in Western Ukraine 11%. Polls have shown that two-thirds of Kyivans supported the ongoing protests.<sup id="cite_ref-FT291213_306-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-FT291213-306">[297]</a></sup>

A poll conducted by the Kucheriv Democratic Initiatives Fund and Razumkov Center, between 20 and 24 December, showed that over 50% of Ukrainians supported the Euromaidan protests, while 42% opposed it.<sup id="cite_ref-razumkov_305-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-razumkov-305">[296]</a></sup>

Another Research & Branding Group survey (conducted from 23 to 27 December) showed that 45% of Ukrainians supported Euromaidan, while 50% did not.<sup id="cite_ref-RBsIU301213_304-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBsIU301213-304">[295]</a></sup> 43% of those polled thought that Euromaidan's consequences "sooner could be negative", while 31% of the respondents thought the opposite; 17% believed that Euromaidan would bring no negative consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-RBsIU301213_304-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBsIU301213-304">[295]</a></sup>

An [Ilko Kucheriv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ilko_Kucheriv&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ilko Kucheriv (page does not exist)") [Democratic Initiatives Foundation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Democratic_Initiatives_Foundation&action=edit&redlink=1 "Democratic Initiatives Foundation (page does not exist)") survey of protesters conducted 7 and 8 December 2013 found that 92% of those who came to Kyiv from across Ukraine came on their own initiative, 6.3% was organised by a public movement, and 1.8% were organised by a party.<sup id="cite_ref-3011crackdownRtP_5-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-3011crackdownRtP-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kp8poll2_314-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kp8poll2-314">[304]</a></sup> 70% Said they came to protest the police brutality of 30 November, and 54% to protest in support of the European Union Association Agreement signing. Among their demands, 82% wanted detained protesters freed, 80% wanted the government to resign, and 75% want president Yanukovych to resign and for snap elections.<sup id="cite_ref-3011crackdownRtP_5-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-3011crackdownRtP-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kp8poll_315-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kp8poll-315">[305]</a></sup> The poll showed that 49.8% of the protesters are residents of Kyiv and 50.2% came from elsewhere in Ukraine. 38% Of the protesters are aged between 15 and 29, 49% are aged between 30 and 54, and 13% are 55 or older. A total of 57.2% of the protesters are men.<sup id="cite_ref-3011crackdownRtP_5-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-3011crackdownRtP-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kp8poll2_314-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-kp8poll2-314">[304]</a></sup>

In the eastern regions of [Donetsk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donetsk "Donetsk"), [Luhansk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luhansk "Luhansk") and [Kharkiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv"), 29% of the population believe "In certain circumstances, an authoritarian regime may be preferable to a democratic one."<sup id="cite_ref-316"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-316">[306]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-317">[307]</a></sup>

According to polls, 11% of the Ukrainian population has participated in the Euromaidan demonstrations, and another 9% has supported the demonstrators with donations.<sup id="cite_ref-318"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-318">[308]</a></sup>

### Public opinion about EU integration

According to a 4 to 9 December 2013 study<sup id="cite_ref-RBpoll491213_303-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RBpoll491213-303">[294]</a></sup> by [Research & Branding Group](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_%26_Branding_Group "Research & Branding Group") 46% of Ukrainians supported the integration of the country into EU, and 36% into the [Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Customs_Union_of_Belarus,_Kazakhstan,_and_Russia "Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia"). Most support for EU integration could be found in West (81%) and in Central (56%) Ukraine; 30% of residents of South Ukraine and 18% of residents of Eastern Ukraine supported the integration with EU as well. Integration with the Customs Union was supported by 61% of East Ukraine and 54% of South Ukraine and also by 22% of Central and 7% of Western Ukraine.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

According to a 7 to 17 December 2013 poll by the [Sociological group "RATING"](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociological_group_%22RATING%22 "Sociological group "RATING""), 49.1% of respondents would vote for Ukraine's accession to the European Union in a referendum, and 29.6% would vote against the motion.<sup id="cite_ref-RspsU251213_319-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RspsU251213-319">[309]</a></sup> Meanwhile, 32.5% of respondents would vote for Ukraine's accession to the [Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Customs_Union_of_Belarus,_Kazakhstan,_and_Russia "Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia"), and 41.9% would vote against.<sup id="cite_ref-RspsU251213_319-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-RspsU251213-319">[309]</a></sup>

### Public opinion about joining the EU

According to an August 2013 study by a [Donetsk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donetsk "Donetsk") company, [Research & Branding Group](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_%26_Branding_Group "Research & Branding Group"),<sup id="cite_ref-320"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-320">[310]</a></sup> 49% of Ukrainians supported signing the Association Agreement, while 31% opposed it and the rest had not decided yet. However, in a December poll by the same company, only 30% claimed that terms of the Association Agreement would be beneficial for the Ukrainian economy, while 39% said they were unfavourable for Ukraine. In the same poll, only 30% said the opposition would be able to stabilise the society and govern the country well, if coming to power, while 37% disagreed.<sup id="cite_ref-321"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-321">[311]</a></sup>

Authors of the [GfK Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/GfK_Ukraine "GfK Ukraine") poll conducted 2–15 October 2013 claim that 45% of respondents believed Ukraine should sign an Association Agreement with the EU, whereas only 14% favoured joining the Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan, and Russia, and 15% preferred non-alignment. Full text of the EU-related question asked by GfK reads, _"Should Ukraine sign the EU-Ukraine Association Agreement, and, in the future, become an EU member?"_<sup id="cite_ref-GfKpoll_322-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-GfKpoll-322">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-323">[313]</a></sup>

Another poll conducted in November by [IFAK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Institute_of_Sociology_IFAK&action=edit&redlink=1 "Institute of Sociology IFAK (page does not exist)") Ukraine for [DW-Trend](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Welle "Deutsche Welle") showed 58% of Ukrainians supporting the country's entry into the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-324">[314]</a></sup> On the other hand, a November 2013 poll by [Kyiv International Institute of Sociology](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv_International_Institute_of_Sociology "Kyiv International Institute of Sociology") showed 39% supporting the country's entry into the European Union and 37% supporting Ukraine's accession to the Customs Union of Belarus, Kazakhstan and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-325">[315]</a></sup>

In December 2013, then [Prime Minister of Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ukraine "Prime Minister of Ukraine") Mykola Azarov refuted the pro-EU poll numbers claiming that many polls posed questions about Ukraine joining the EU, and that Ukraine [had never been invited](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_relations "Ukraine–European Union relations") to join the Union,<sup id="cite_ref-326"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-326">[316]</a></sup> but only to sign the [European Union Association Agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement "European Union Association Agreement") (a treaty between the EU and another country, in this case Ukraine).<sup id="cite_ref-327"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-327">[317]</a></sup>

### Comparison with the Orange Revolution

| External image |
| --- |
|   [The writing on the wall «Revolution»](https://i.pinimg.com/originals/31/25/7c/31257c10856573f598c8099fb8710b77.jpg) |

The pro-European Union protests were Ukraine's largest since the [Orange Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orange_Revolution "Orange Revolution") of 2004, which saw Yanukovych forced to resign as prime minister over voting irregularities. Although comparing the 2013 events in the same [East](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_world#European_concepts "Eastern world")\-[West](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world") vector as 2004, with Ukraine remaining "a key geopolitical prize in eastern Europe" for Russia and the EU, _[The Moscow Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Moscow_Times "The Moscow Times")_ noted that Yanukovych's government was in a significantly stronger position following [his election in 2010](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Ukrainian_presidential_election "2010 Ukrainian presidential election").<sup id="cite_ref-328"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-328">[318]</a></sup> The _[Financial Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Times "Financial Times")_ said the 2013 protests were "largely spontaneous, sparked by social media, and have caught Ukraine's political opposition unprepared" compared to their well-organised predecessors.<sup id="cite_ref-329"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-329">[319]</a></sup> The hashtag #euromaidan ([Ukrainian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_language "Ukrainian language"): #євромайдан, [Russian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): #евромайдан), emerged immediately on the first meeting of the protests and was highly useful as a communication instrument for protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_330-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-330">[320]</a></sup> [Vitali Klitschko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitali_Klitschko "Vitali Klitschko") wrote in a tweet<sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-331">[321]</a></sup> "Friends! All those who came to Maydan \[Independence Square\], well done! Who has not done it yet – join us now!" The protest hashtag also gained traction on the VKontakte social media network, and Klitschko tweeted a link to a speech<sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-332">[322]</a></sup> he made on the square saying that once the protest was 100,000-strong, "we'll go for Yanukovych" – referring to President Viktor Yanukovych.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_330-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-330">[320]</a></sup>

In an interview, opposition leader Yuriy Lutsenko, when asked if the current opposition was weaker than it was in 2004, argued that the opposition was stronger because the stakes were higher, "I asked each \[of the opposition leaders\]: 'Do you realise that this is not a protest? It is a revolution \[...\] we have two roads – we go to prison or we win.'"<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-333">[323]</a></sup>

[Paul Robert Magocsi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Robert_Magocsi "Paul Robert Magocsi") illustrated the effect of the Orange Revolution on Euromaidan, saying,

> Was the Orange Revolution a genuine revolution? Yes it was. And we see the effects today. The revolution wasn't a revolution of the streets or a revolution of (political) elections; it was a revolution of the minds of people, in the sense that for the first time in a long time, Ukrainians and people living in territorial Ukraine saw the opportunity to protest and change their situation. This was a profound change in the character of the population of the former Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-334">[324]</a></sup>

[Lviv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lviv "Lviv")\-based historian [Yaroslav Hrytsak](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yaroslav_Hrytsak "Yaroslav Hrytsak") also remarked on the generational shift,

> This is a revolution of the generation that we call the contemporaries of Ukraine's independence (who were born around the time of 1991); it is more similar to the [Occupy Wall Street protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupy_movement "Occupy movement") or those in [Istanbul demonstrations (of this year)](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gezi_Park_protests "Gezi Park protests"). It's a revolution of young people who are very educated, people who are active in social media, who are mobile and 90 percent of whom have university degrees, but who don't have futures.<sup id="cite_ref-KPUEM2711_112-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-KPUEM2711-112">[106]</a></sup>

According to Hrytsak: "Young Ukrainians resemble young Italians, Czech, Poles, or Germans more than they resemble Ukrainians who are 50 and older. This generation has a stronger desire for European integration and fewer regional divides than their seniors."<sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-335">[325]</a></sup> In a Kyiv International Institute of Sociology poll taken in September, joining the European Union was mostly supported by young Ukrainians (69.8% of those aged 18 to 29), higher than the national average of 43.2% support.<sup id="cite_ref-whichunion_336-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-whichunion-336">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-337">[327]</a></sup> A November 2013 poll by the same institute found the same result with 70.8% aged 18 to 29 wanting to join the European Union while 39.7% was the national average of support.<sup id="cite_ref-whichunion_336-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-whichunion-336">[326]</a></sup> An opinion poll by [GfK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/GfK "GfK") conducted 2–15 October found that among respondents aged 16–29 with a position on integration, 73% favoured signing an Association Agreement with the EU, while only 45% of those over the age of 45 favoured Association. The lowest support for European integration was among people with incomplete secondary and higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-GfKpoll_322-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-GfKpoll-322">[312]</a></sup>

### Escalation to violence

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hrushevskyi_street_-_2014_Jan_22_-_28.jpg)

Clashes on Hrushevskyi Street in Kyiv, 22 January 2014

The movement started peacefully but violence broke out, especially in January and February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-338"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-338">[328]</a></sup> The [Associated Press](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associated_Press "Associated Press") said on 19 February 2014:

> The latest bout of street violence began Tuesday when protesters attacked police lines and set fires outside parliament, accusing Yanukovych of ignoring their demands to enact constitutional reforms that would limit the president's power—a key opposition demand. Parliament, dominated by his supporters, was stalling on taking up a constitutional reform to limit presidential powers. Police responded by attacking the protest camp. Armed with water cannons, stun grenades and rubber bullets, police dismantled some barricades. But the protesters held their ground through the night, encircling the protest camp with new burning barricades of tires, furniture and debris.<sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-339">[329]</a></sup>

In the early stages of Euromaidan, there was discussion about whether the Euromaidan movement constituted a revolution. At the time many protest leaders (such as [Oleh Tyahnybok](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oleh_Tyahnybok "Oleh Tyahnybok")) had already used this term frequently when addressing the public. Tyahnybok called in an official 2 December press release for police officers and members of the military to defect to 'the Ukrainian revolution'.<sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-340">[330]</a></sup>

In a [Skype](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skype "Skype") interview with media analyst Andrij Holovatyj, [Vitaly Portnikov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitaly_Portnikov "Vitaly Portnikov"), Council Member of the "Maidan" National Alliance and President and Editor-in-Chief of the Ukrainian television channel [TVi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/TVi_(channel) "TVi (channel)"), stated "EuroMaidan is a revolution and revolutions can drag on for years" and that "what is happening in Ukraine goes much deeper. It is changing the national fabric of Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-341">[331]</a></sup>

On 10 December Yanukovych said, "Calls for a revolution pose a threat to national security."<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-342">[332]</a></sup> Former [Georgian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_(country) "Georgia (country)") president [Mikhail Saakashvili](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Saakashvili "Mikhail Saakashvili") has described the movement as "the first geopolitical revolution of the 21st century".<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-343">[333]</a></sup>

Political expert [Anders Åslund](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders_%C3%85slund "Anders Åslund") commented on this aspect,

> Revolutionary times have their own logic that is very different from the logic of ordinary politics, as writers from [Alexis de Tocqueville](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville "Alexis de Tocqueville") to [Crane Brinton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crane_Brinton "Crane Brinton") have taught. The first thing to understand about Ukraine today is that it has entered a revolutionary stage. Like it or not, we had better deal with the new environment rationally.<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-344">[334]</a></sup>

## Impact

### Political impact

During the annual [World Economic Forum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Economic_Forum "World Economic Forum") meeting at the end of January 2014 in [Davos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davos "Davos") ([Switzerland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland")) [Ukrainian Prime Minister](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Prime_Minister "Ukrainian Prime Minister") [Mykola Azarov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mykola_Azarov "Mykola Azarov") received no invitations to the main events; according to the _[Financial Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Times "Financial Times")'_s [Gideon Rachman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gideon_Rachman "Gideon Rachman") because the Ukrainian government was blamed for the violence of the [2014 Hrushevskoho Street riots](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Hrushevskoho_Street_riots "2014 Hrushevskoho Street riots").<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-345">[335]</a></sup>

A telephone call was leaked of US diplomat [Victoria Nuland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victoria_Nuland "Victoria Nuland") speaking to the [US Ambassador to Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Ambassador_to_Ukraine "US Ambassador to Ukraine"), [Geoffrey Pyatt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoffrey_R._Pyatt "Geoffrey R. Pyatt") about the future of the country, in which she said that [Klitschko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitali_Klitschko "Vitali Klitschko") should not be in the future government, and expressed her preference for [Arseniy Yatsenyuk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arseniy_Yatsenyuk "Arseniy Yatsenyuk"), who became interim Prime Minister. She also casually stated "fuck the EU."<sup id="cite_ref-346"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-346">[336]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-347">[337]</a></sup> German chancellor [Angela Merkel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel "Angela Merkel") said she deemed Nuland's comment "completely unacceptable".<sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-348">[338]</a></sup> Commenting on the situation afterwards, State Department spokeswoman [Jen Psaki](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jen_Psaki "Jen Psaki") said that Nuland had apologized to her EU counterparts<sup id="cite_ref-349"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-349">[339]</a></sup> while [White House](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House") spokesman [Jay Carney](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay_Carney "Jay Carney") alleged that because it had been "tweeted out by the Russian government, it says something about Russia's role".<sup id="cite_ref-GarVNF_350-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-GarVNF-350">[340]</a></sup>

In February 2014 _IBTimes_ reported, "if [Svoboda](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svoboda_(political_party) "Svoboda (political party)") and other far-right groups gain greater exposure through their involvement in the protests, there are fears they could gain more sympathy and support from a public grown weary of political corruption and Russian influence on Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-351">[341]</a></sup> In the following late October [2014 Ukrainian parliamentary election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_parliamentary_election "2014 Ukrainian parliamentary election") Svoboda lost 31 seats of the 37 seats it had won in the [2012 parliamentary election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Ukrainian_parliamentary_election "2012 Ukrainian parliamentary election").<sup id="cite_ref-allcountedCECIU81114_352-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-allcountedCECIU81114-352">[342]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CESOlszańskiUKel12_353-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-CESOlsza%C5%84skiUKel12-353">[343]</a></sup> The other main far-right party [Right Sector](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_Sector "Right Sector") won 1 seat (of the 450 seats in the [Ukrainian parliament](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_parliament "Ukrainian parliament")) in the same 2014 election.<sup id="cite_ref-allcountedCECIU81114_352-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-allcountedCECIU81114-352">[342]</a></sup> From 27 February 2014 till 12 November 2014 three members of Svoboda did hold positions in [Ukraine's government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Yatsenyuk_Government "First Yatsenyuk Government").<sup id="cite_ref-Svoboda_party_members_in_Ukrainian_government_resign_354-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-Svoboda_party_members_in_Ukrainian_government_resign-354">[344]</a></sup>

On 21 February, after negotiations between President Yanukovych and representatives of opposition with mediation of representatives of the European Union and Russia, the agreement "About settlement of political crisis in Ukraine" was signed. The agreement provided return to the constitution of 2004, that is to a parliamentary presidential government, carrying out early elections of the president until the end of 2014 and formation of "the government of national trust".<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-355">[345]</a></sup> The Verkhovna Rada adopted the law on release of all detainees during protest actions. Divisions of "Golden eagle" and internal troops left the center of Kyiv. On 21 February, at the public announcement leaders of parliamentary opposition of conditions of the signed Agreement, representatives of "Right Sector" declared that they don't accept the gradualness of political reforms stipulated in the document, and demanded immediate resignation of the president Yanukovych—otherwise they intended to go for storm of Presidential Administration and Verkhovna Rada.<sup id="cite_ref-356"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-356">[346]</a></sup>

On the night of 22 February activists of Euromaidan seized the government quarter<sup id="cite_ref-357"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-357">[347]</a></sup> left by law enforcement authorities and made a number of new demands—in particular, immediate resignation of the president Yanukovych.<sup id="cite_ref-358"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-358">[348]</a></sup> Earlier that day, they stormed into Yanukovych's mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-359"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-359">[349]</a></sup>

On 23 February 2014, following the 2014 Ukrainian revolution, the Rada passed a bill that would have altered the [law on languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legislation_on_languages_in_Ukraine "Legislation on languages in Ukraine") of minorities, including Russian. The bill would have made Ukrainian the sole state language at all levels.<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-360">[350]</a></sup> However, on the next week 1 March, President Turchynov vetoed the bill.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_language_veto_361-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-nytimes_language_veto-361">[351]</a></sup>

Following the Protests, Euromaidan activists mobilized toward state transformation. Activists began to, "promote reforms, drafting and advocating for legislative proposals and monitoring reform implementations."<sup id="cite_ref-362"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-362">[352]</a></sup>

### Economic impact

The Prime Minister, Mykola Azarov, asked for 20 billion Euros (US$27 billion) in loans and aid from the EU<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_162-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-autogenerated3-162">[153]</a></sup> The EU was willing to offer 610 million euros (838 million US) in loans,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_163-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-autogenerated1-163">[154]</a></sup> however Russia was willing to offer 15 billion US in loans.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_163-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-autogenerated1-163">[154]</a></sup> Russia also offered Ukraine cheaper gas prices.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_163-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-autogenerated1-163">[154]</a></sup> As a condition for the loans, the EU required major changes to the regulations and laws in Ukraine. Russia did not.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_162-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-autogenerated3-162">[153]</a></sup>

[Moody's Investors Service](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service "Moody's Investors Service") reported on 4 December 2013 "As a consequence of the severity of the protests, demand for foreign currency is likely to rise" and noted that this was another blow to Ukraine's already poor [solvency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solvency "Solvency").<sup id="cite_ref-363"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-363">[353]</a></sup> First deputy Prime Minister [Serhiy Arbuzov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serhiy_Arbuzov "Serhiy Arbuzov") stated on 7 December Ukraine risked a [default](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Default_(finance) "Default (finance)") if it failed to raise $10 billion "I asked for a loan to support us, and Europe \[the EU\] agreed, but a mistake was made – we failed to put it on paper."<sup id="cite_ref-SAIU71213_364-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-SAIU71213-364">[354]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Petro_Poroshenko_addresses_Euromaidan.jpg)

[Petro Poroshenko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko "Petro Poroshenko") addresses Euromaidan on 8 December 2013

On 3 December, Azarov warned that Ukraine might not be able to fulfill its [natural gas contracts with Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Ukraine#Prices_of_import "Natural gas in Ukraine").<sup id="cite_ref-gaspA31213_365-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-gaspA31213-365">[355]</a></sup> And he blamed the [deal on restoring gas supplies of 18 January 2009](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Russia%E2%80%93Ukraine_gas_dispute#Crisis_resolved "2009 Russia–Ukraine gas dispute") for this.<sup id="cite_ref-gaspA31213_365-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-gaspA31213-365">[355]</a></sup>

On 5 December, Prime Minister [Mykola Azarov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mykola_Azarov "Mykola Azarov") stated that "money to finance the payment of pensions, wages, social payments, support of the operation of the housing and utility sector and medical institutions do not appear due to unrest in the streets" and he added that authorities were doing everything possible to ensure the timely financing of them.<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-366">[356]</a></sup> [Minister of Social Policy of Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Social_Policy_(Ukraine) "Ministry of Social Policy (Ukraine)") [Natalia Korolevska](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natalia_Korolevska "Natalia Korolevska") stated on 2 January 2014 that these January 2014 payments would begin according to schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-367"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-367">[357]</a></sup>

On 11 December, the [second Azarov Government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Azarov_Government "Second Azarov Government") postponed social payments due to "the temporarily blocking of the government".<sup id="cite_ref-368"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-368">[358]</a></sup> The same day [Reuters](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reuters "Reuters") commented (when talking about Euromaidan) "The crisis has added to the financial hardship of a country on the brink of bankruptcy" and added that (at the time) investors thought it more likely than not that Ukraine would default over the next five years (since it then cost Ukraine over US$1 million a year to insure $10 million in state debt).<sup id="cite_ref-369"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-369">[359]</a></sup>

[Fitch Ratings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitch_Ratings "Fitch Ratings") reported on 16 December that the (political) "standoff" had led to "greater the risk that political uncertainty will raise demand for foreign currency, causing additional reserve losses and increasing the risk of disorderly currency movement".<sup id="cite_ref-FitchIU161213_370-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-FitchIU161213-370">[360]</a></sup> It also added "Interest rates rose sharply as the National Bank sought to tighten hryvnia liquidity."<sup id="cite_ref-FitchIU161213_370-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-FitchIU161213-370">[360]</a></sup>

First Deputy Finance Minister [Anatoliy Miarkovsky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Anatoliy_Miarkovsky&action=edit&redlink=1 "Anatoliy Miarkovsky (page does not exist)") stated on 17 December the Ukrainian [government budget deficit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_budget_deficit "Government budget deficit") in 2014 could amount to about 3% with a "plus or minus" [deviation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deviation_(statistics) "Deviation (statistics)") of 0.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-371"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-371">[361]</a></sup>

On 18 December, the day after [an economical agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/17_December_2013_Ukrainian%E2%80%93Russian_action_plan "17 December 2013 Ukrainian–Russian action plan") with Russia was signed, Prime Minister [Mykola Azarov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mykola_Azarov "Mykola Azarov") stated, "Nothing is threatening stability of the financial-economic situation in Ukraine now. Not a single economic factor."<sup id="cite_ref-372"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-372">[362]</a></sup> However, [BBC News](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_News "BBC News") reported that the deal "will not fix Ukraine's deeper economic problems" in an article titled "Russian bailout masks Ukraine's economic mess".<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-373">[363]</a></sup>

On 21 January 2014, the [Kyiv City State Administration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv_City_State_Administration "Kyiv City State Administration") claimed that protests in Kyiv had so far caused the city more than 2 million US dollars worth of damage.<sup id="cite_ref-XNAU21114_374-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-XNAU21114-374">[364]</a></sup> It intended to claim compensation for damage caused by all demonstrators, regardless of their political affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-XNAU21114_374-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-XNAU21114-374">[364]</a></sup>

On 5 February 2014, the hryvnia fell to a five-year low against the US dollar.<sup id="cite_ref-375"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-375">[365]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%84%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD_02_%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_2014_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%97%D0%B2.JPG)

Kyiv, 2 February 2014

On 21 February 2014, [Standard & Poor's](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s "Standard & Poor's") cut Ukraine's credit rating to [CCC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s#Long-term_credit_ratings "Standard & Poor's"); adding that the country risked default without "significantly favourable changes".<sup id="cite_ref-376"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-376">[366]</a></sup> Standard & Poor's analysts believed the [compromise deal of the same day between President Yanukovych and the opposition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_2014_Euromaidan_riots#Deal "February 2014 Euromaidan riots") made it "less likely Ukraine would receive desperately needed Russian aid, thereby increasing the risk of default on its debts".<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-377">[367]</a></sup>

In Kyiv, life continued "as normal" outside the "protest zone" (namely [Maidan Nezalezhnosti](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maidan_Nezalezhnosti "Maidan Nezalezhnosti")).<sup id="cite_ref-378"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-378">[368]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-379">[369]</a></sup>

Before the Euromaidan demonstrations happened, Ukrainians did not have a strong and unified understanding of what it meant to be Ukrainian. There was confusion on whether a person should be considered Ukrainian on a civic or ethnographic basis. Most citizens of Ukraine during the Euromaidan perceived the protests as a battle against the regime. Therefore, the social impact that Euromaidan had on Ukrainians is a stronger sense of national identity and unity. Results from a survey shows that the people who identified themselves as Ukrainian after the Euromaidan grew by 10% compared to the survey conducted before the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-380"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-380">[370]</a></sup>

"Euromaidan" was named [Word of the Year](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_of_the_Year "Word of the Year") for 2013 by [modern Ukrainian language](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Ukrainian_language "Modern Ukrainian language") and slang dictionary Myslovo,<sup id="cite_ref-381"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-381">[371]</a></sup> and the most popular [neologism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neologism "Neologism") in Russia by web analytics company Public.ru.<sup id="cite_ref-382"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-382">[372]</a></sup>

### Cultural impact

According to a representative of the Kyiv History Museum, its collection in the [Ukrainian House](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_House "Ukrainian House") on the night of 18–19 February, after it was recaptured by the police from the protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-383"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-383">[373]</a></sup> Eyewitnesses report seeing the police forces plundering and destroying the museum's property.<sup id="cite_ref-384"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-384">[374]</a></sup>

#### Music of Maidan

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Protester_Piano_Extremist_plays_on_the_roof_burned_%22Berkut%22_bus._The_barricade_across_Hrushevskoho_str._Kiev,_10.02.2014..jpg)

Protester performs on the roof of burned "[Berkut](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berkut_(special_police_force) "Berkut (special police force)")" bus. The barricade across Hrushevskoho str. Kyiv, 10 February 2014.

Leading Ukrainian performers sang the song "Brat za Brata" (English: "Brother for Brother") by Kozak System to support protesters. The song was one of the unofficial anthems of Euromaidan.<sup id="cite_ref-385"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-385">[375]</a></sup>

Ukrainian-Polish band Taraka came up with a song dedicated to "Euromaidan" "Podaj Rękę Ukrainie" (Give a Hand to Ukraine). The song uses the first several words of the [National anthem of Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_anthem_of_Ukraine "National anthem of Ukraine") "Ukraine has not yet died".<sup id="cite_ref-386"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-386">[376]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-387"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-387">[377]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-388">[378]</a></sup>

Among other tunes, some remakes of the Ukrainian folk song "Aflame the pine was on fire" appeared ([Ukrainian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_language "Ukrainian language"): Горіла сосна, палала).<sup id="cite_ref-389"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-389">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-390">[380]</a></sup>

The Ukrainian band Skriabin created a song dedicated to the revolutionary days of Maidan.<sup id="cite_ref-391"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-391">[381]</a></sup> Another native of Kyiv dedicated a song to [titushky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titushky "Titushky").<sup id="cite_ref-392"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-392">[382]</a></sup>

[DJ Rudy Paulenko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=DJ_Rudy_Paulenko&action=edit&redlink=1 "DJ Rudy Paulenko (page does not exist)") created a track inspired by events on Maidan called "The Battle at Maidan".<sup id="cite_ref-393"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-393">[383]</a></sup>

[Belarusian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus") rock band [Lyapis Trubetskoy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyapis_Trubetskoy "Lyapis Trubetskoy")'s song "Warriors of Light" (_Voiny Svieta_) was one of the unofficial anthems of Maidan.<sup id="cite_ref-394"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-394">[384]</a></sup>

#### Films on Maidan

A compilation of short films about the 2013 revolution named [Babylon'13](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylon%2713 "Babylon'13") was created.<sup id="cite_ref-395"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-395">[385]</a></sup>

Polish and Ukrainian activists created a short film, "Happy Kyiv", editing it with the [Pharrell Williams](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharrell_Williams "Pharrell Williams") hit "[Happy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Happy_(Pharrell_Williams_song) "Happy (Pharrell Williams song)")" and some shoots of Babylon'13.<sup id="cite_ref-396"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-396">[386]</a></sup>

On 5 February 2014, a group of activist cinematographers initiated a series of films about the people of Euromaidan.<sup id="cite_ref-397"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-397">[387]</a></sup>

The American filmmaker [John Beck Hofmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Beck_Hofmann "John Beck Hofmann") made the film _[Maidan Massacre](https://www.imdb.com/title/tt4052016/)_, about the sniper shootings. It premiered at the Siena International Film Festival, receiving the Audience Award.<sup id="cite_ref-398"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-398">[388]</a></sup>

In 2014 Belarusian-Ukrainian filmmaker [Sergei Loznitsa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergei_Loznitsa "Sergei Loznitsa") released the documentary _[Maidan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maidan_(2014_film) "Maidan (2014 film)")_. It was filmed by several cameramen instructed by Loznitsa during the revolution in 2013 and 2014 and depicts different aspects, from peaceful rallies to the bloody clashes between police and protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-399"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-399">[389]</a></sup>

In 2015 Netflix released the documentary _[Winter on Fire: Ukraine's Fight for Freedom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_on_Fire:_Ukraine%27s_Fight_for_Freedom "Winter on Fire: Ukraine's Fight for Freedom")_ about the Euromaidan protests. The documentary shows the protests from the start until the resignation of Viktor Yanukovych. The movie won the Grolsch People's Choice Documentary Award at the 2015 Toronto International Film Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-400"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-400">[390]</a></sup>

In 2016 the documentary _[Ukraine on Fire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine_on_Fire_(2016_film) "Ukraine on Fire (2016 film)")_ premiered at the [Taormina Film Fest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taormina_Film_Fest "Taormina Film Fest").<sup id="cite_ref-401"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-401">[391]</a></sup> The central thesis of the film is that the events that led to the flight of Yanukovych in February 2014 were a [coup d'état](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Coup d'état") led by the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-402"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-402">[392]</a></sup>

_[The Long Breakup](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Long_Breakup "The Long Breakup")_ premiered at the 2020 East Oregon Film Festival. This long term documentary about complex relationship between Ukraine and Russia tells about the Euromaidan and the Orange Revolution and moreover from the Crimea annexation and the Donbass War.<sup id="cite_ref-403"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-403">[393]</a></sup>

#### Visual Arts at Maidan

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Performance_%22Artist-fighter%22._.jpg)

Performance "artist-fighter"

The protests attracted numerous photographers who documented everyday life and symbolic moments at Maidan.<sup id="cite_ref-404"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-404">[394]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-405"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-405">[395]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-406"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-406">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-407"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-407">[397]</a></sup> The Maidan portest also attract support by visual artists including illustrator Sasha Godiayeva<sup id="cite_ref-408"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-408">[398]</a></sup> and the painter [Temo Svirely](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temo_Svirely "Temo Svirely").<sup id="cite_ref-409"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-409">[399]</a></sup>

**Theatre**

While many Ukrainian playwrights and directors had trained and worked in Russia during the 1990s and 2000s, for lack of opportunity in their home country, an increasing number of them - such as Natalia Vorozhbit and Maksim Kyrochkin - decided to return to Ukraine after the Euromaidan, to contribute to an emerging vibrant field of new drama, or Ukrainian New Drama.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_410-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-:0-410">[400]</a></sup> There was also a noticeable shift towards writing in Ukrainian after 2014, whereas some bilingual Ukrainian dramatists had used Russian prior to 2014 in order to serve a greater audience base. Vorozhbit wrote a highly significant play about the Euromaidan, _The Maidan Diaries_, which opened at the Franko National Theatre (one of Ukraine's two national theatres; Franko is the Ukrainian language national theatre).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_410-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-:0-410">[400]</a></sup>

### Sport

The [2013–14 UEFA Europa League](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League "2013–14 UEFA Europa League") [Round of 32](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League_knockout_phase "2013–14 UEFA Europa League knockout phase") match of 20 February 2014 between [FC Dynamo Kyiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv "FC Dynamo Kyiv") and [Valencia CF](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valencia_CF "Valencia CF") was moved by [UEFA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA "UEFA") from [Kyiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv "Kyiv")'s [Olimpiyskiy National Sports Complex](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olimpiyskiy_National_Sports_Complex "Olimpiyskiy National Sports Complex") to the [GSP Stadium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/GSP_Stadium "GSP Stadium") in [Nicosia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicosia "Nicosia"), [Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus"), "due to the security situation in the Ukrainian capital".<sup id="cite_ref-411"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-411">[401]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-412"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-412">[402]</a></sup>

On 19 February, the [Ukrainian athletes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine_at_the_2014_Winter_Olympics "Ukraine at the 2014 Winter Olympics") competing in the [2014 Winter Olympics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics "2014 Winter Olympics") asked for and were refused permission by the [International Olympic Committee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee "International Olympic Committee") (IOC) to wear black arm bands to honour those killed in the [violent clashes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution "2014 Ukrainian revolution") in Kyiv.<sup id="cite_ref-R19214Umb_413-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-R19214Umb-413">[403]</a></sup> IOC president [Thomas Bach](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Bach "Thomas Bach") offered his condolences "to those who have lost loved ones in these tragic events".<sup id="cite_ref-R19214Umb_413-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-R19214Umb-413">[403]</a></sup>

On 19 February 2014, [alpine skier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_skier "Alpine skier") [Bohdana Matsotska](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohdana_Matsotska "Bohdana Matsotska") refused to further participate in the [2014 Winter Olympics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics "2014 Winter Olympics") in protest against the [violent clashes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution "2014 Ukrainian revolution") in [Kyiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv "Kyiv").<sup id="cite_ref-KPBS19214_414-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-KPBS19214-414">[404]</a></sup> She and her father posted a message on [Facebook](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook "Facebook") stating "In solidarity with the fighters on the barricades of the Maidan, and as a protest against the criminal actions made towards the protesters, the irresponsibility of the president and his lackey government, we refuse further performance at the Olympic Games in Sochi 2014."<sup id="cite_ref-KPBS19214_414-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-KPBS19214-414">[404]</a></sup>

On 4 March 2014, the [2013–14 Eurocup Basketball](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Eurocup_Basketball "2013–14 Eurocup Basketball") [Round of 16](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Eurocup_Basketball_Knockout_Stage "2013–14 Eurocup Basketball Knockout Stage") game between [BC Budivelnyk Kyiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BC_Budivelnyk "BC Budivelnyk") and [JSF Nanterre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/JSF_Nanterre "JSF Nanterre") was moved to [Žalgiris Arena](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%BDalgiris_Arena "Žalgiris Arena") in [Kaunas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaunas "Kaunas"), [Lithuania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania"). On 5 March 2014, another [Round of 16](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Eurocup_Basketball_Knockout_Stage "2013–14 Eurocup Basketball Knockout Stage") game between [Khimik Yuzhny](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BC_Khimik "BC Khimik") and [Aykon TED Ankara](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_Ankara_Kolejliler "TED Ankara Kolejliler") was moved to [Abdi Ipekci Arena](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i_Arena "Abdi İpekçi Arena") in [Istanbul](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul").<sup id="cite_ref-415"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-415">[405]</a></sup>

### Legacy

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Euromaidan_coin_r.jpg)

Coin [commemorating](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_commemorative_coins_of_Ukraine "List of commemorative coins of Ukraine") the Euromaidan, 2015.

In mid-October 2014, President [Petro Poroshenko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petro_Poroshenko "Petro Poroshenko") stated that 21 November (Euromaidan started on 21 November 2013) will be celebrated as "Day of Dignity and Freedom".<sup id="cite_ref-late_at_night_IU_171-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-late_at_night_IU-171">[162]</a></sup>

As of February 2019, the Ukrainian government has broken ground on a new Maidan memorial that will run the length of [Instytutska Street](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instytutska_Street "Instytutska Street"), now also known as Avenue of the Heavenly Hundred.<sup id="cite_ref-416"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-416">[406]</a></sup>

On 10 January 2022 [Russian President](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_President "Russian President") [Vladimir Putin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin") claimed that the protesters of the [2022 Kazakh protests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Kazakh_protests "2022 Kazakh protests") had used "Maidan technologies".<sup id="cite_ref-417"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-417">[407]</a></sup>

## Slogans and symbols

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Blue_and_yellow_ribbon.svg)

The Ukrainian ribbon. Ribbons are common symbols of non-violent protest

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_rally_on_European_Square_in_Kiev_on_Sunday,_November_24,_2013_(cropped).jpg)

The rally on European Square in Kyiv, 24 November 2013

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Headquarters_of_the_Euromaidan_revolution.jpg)

Headquarters of the Euromaidan. At the front entrance there is a portrait of [Stepan Bandera](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stepan_Bandera "Stepan Bandera"), a twentieth century Ukrainian nationalist.

A chant that was commonly chanted among protesters was “Slava Ukraini! Heroiam slava!” - "[Glory to Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glory_to_Ukraine "Glory to Ukraine"), Glory to Heroes!"<sup id="cite_ref-cska_418-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-cska-418">[408]</a></sup> The chant has extended beyond Ukrainians and has been used by [Crimean Tatars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatars "Crimean Tatars") and [Russians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russians "Russians").<sup id="cite_ref-cska_418-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-cska-418">[408]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-419"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-419">[409]</a></sup>

The red-and-black [battle flag](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_flag "War flag") of the [Ukrainian Insurgent Army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army "Ukrainian Insurgent Army") (UPA) is another popular symbol among protesters, and the wartime insurgents have acted as a large inspiration for Euromaidan protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-420"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-420">[410]</a></sup> Serhy Yekelchyk of the [University of Victoria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Victoria "University of Victoria") says the use of UPA imagery and slogans was more of a potent symbol of protest against the current government and Russia rather than adulation for the insurgents themselves, explaining "The reason for the sudden prominence of \[UPA symbolism\] in Kyiv is that it is the strongest possible expression of protest against the pro-Russian orientation of the current government."<sup id="cite_ref-421"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-421">[411]</a></sup> The colours of the flag symbolise Ukrainian red blood spilled on Ukrainian [black earth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chernozem "Chernozem").<sup id="cite_ref-422"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-422">[412]</a></sup>

## Reactions

In a poll published on 24 February 2014 by the state-owned [Russian Public Opinion Research Center](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Public_Opinion_Research_Center "Russian Public Opinion Research Center"), only 15% of those Russians polled said 'yes' to the question: "Should Russia react to the overthrow of the legally elected authorities in Ukraine?"<sup id="cite_ref-423"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-423">[413]</a></sup>

## Legal hearings and investigation

Investigation about Euromaidan was ongoing since December 2013 following the initial dispersal of student gathering on the night of 30 November. On 13 December 2013 the President [Viktor Yanukovych](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych "Viktor Yanukovych") and government officials announced that three high-ranking officials will be brought to justice.<sup id="cite_ref-424"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-424">[414]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-425"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-425">[415]</a></sup> The [General Prosecutor's Office of Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prosecutor_General_of_Ukraine "Prosecutor General of Ukraine") questioned a chairman of the Kyiv City State Administration [Oleksandr Popov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oleksandr_Popov "Oleksandr Popov") on 13 December and a Security Council secretary [Andriy Klyuev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andriy_Klyuev "Andriy Klyuev") on 16 December.<sup id="cite_ref-426"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-426">[416]</a></sup> The announcement about ongoing investigation became public at the so-called "round table" negotiations initiated by former Ukrainian President [Leonid Kravchuk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Kravchuk "Leonid Kravchuk").<sup id="cite_ref-427"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-427">[417]</a></sup> On 14 December, both Sivkovych and Popov were officially temporarily relieved of their duties until conclusion of the investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-428"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-428">[418]</a></sup>

On 17 December the Prosecutor General questioned an activist [Ruslana Lyzhychko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruslana_Lyzhychko "Ruslana Lyzhychko") who informed that beside Popov under pre-trial investigation are Sivkovych, Koriak and Fedchuk.<sup id="cite_ref-429"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-429">[419]</a></sup> On request of parliamentary opposition, Prosecutor General [Viktor Pshonka](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Pshonka "Viktor Pshonka") read in [Verkhovna Rada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada "Verkhovna Rada") (Ukrainian parliament) a report on investigation about dispersal of protesters on 30 November.<sup id="cite_ref-430"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-430">[420]</a></sup> During the report the Prosecutor General acknowledged that members of [public order militsiya "Berkut"](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berkut_(special_police_force) "Berkut (special police force)") "exceeded the use of force" after being provoked by protesters. Pshonka also noted that investigation has not yet determined who exactly ordered use of force.<sup id="cite_ref-431"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-431">[421]</a></sup> Following the PG's report, the parliamentary opposition registered a statement on creation of provisional investigation committee in regards to actions of law enforcement agencies towards peaceful protests in Kyiv.<sup id="cite_ref-432"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-432">[422]</a></sup>

Earlier, a separate investigation was started by the [Security Service of Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine "Security Service of Ukraine") on 8 December 2013 about actions aimed at seizing state power in Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-433"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-433">[423]</a></sup> In the context of the [1 December 2013 Euromaidan riots](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1_December_2013_Euromaidan_riots "1 December 2013 Euromaidan riots"), the Prosecutor General informed that in calls for the overthrow of the government are involved member of radical groups.<sup id="cite_ref-434"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-434">[424]</a></sup> During the events at Bankova, the Ukrainian militsiya managed to detained 9 people and after few days the Ministry of Internal Affairs announced that it considers Ukrainian organization Bratstvo (see [Dmytro Korchynsky](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmytro_Korchynsky "Dmytro Korchynsky")) to be involved in instigation of disorders, while no one out of the detained were members of that organization.<sup id="cite_ref-435"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-435">[425]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-436"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-436">[426]</a></sup>

Ukrainian mass media reported the results of forensic examinations, according to which, the government police Berkut was implicated in the murders of maidan protesters since, according to these forensic examinations, matches were found between the bullets extracted from the bodies of maidan protesters and the weapons of the government police Berkut.<sup id="cite_ref-437"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-437">[427]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-438"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-438">[428]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-439"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-439">[429]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-440"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-440">[430]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-441"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-441">[431]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-442"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-442">[432]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zmina.info_443-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-zmina.info-443">[433]</a></sup> The experts explained why no match between the bullets and the weapons, which had been assigned to the Berkut special force, had been found as a result of the examination of the bullets held in January 2015, whereas the examination carried out in December of the same year had showed such a match.<sup id="cite_ref-zmina.info_443-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-zmina.info-443">[433]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-444"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-444">[434]</a></sup>
