## Notes

1.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-13 "Jump up")** Since 1 December 2013 Kyiv's Town Hall has been occupied by Euromaidan protesters; this forced the [Kyiv City Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv_City_Council "Kyiv City Council") to meet in the [Solomianka Raion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomianka_Raion "Solomianka Raion") state administration building instead.<sup id="cite_ref-12"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-20 "Jump up")** There was no legal basis for these bans since in Ukraine only a court can ban the activities of a political force.<sup id="cite_ref-19"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
3.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-49 "Jump up")** Reports of some protesters attending under duress from superiors
4.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-54 "Jump up")** _Titushky_ are provocators during protests.<sup id="cite_ref-53"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup>
5.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-62 "Jump up")** Early November 2012 [Communist Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Ukraine "Communist Party of Ukraine") party leader [Petro Symonenko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petro_Symonenko "Petro Symonenko") stated that his party will not co-operate with other parties in the new parliament elected in the [2012 Ukrainian parliamentary election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Ukrainian_parliamentary_election "2012 Ukrainian parliamentary election").<sup id="cite_ref-60"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> Nevertheless, in [at the time in parliament](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/7th_Ukrainian_Verkhovna_Rada "7th Ukrainian Verkhovna Rada") its parliamentary faction usually voted similarly to the [Party of Regions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party_of_Regions "Party of Regions") parliamentary faction.<sup id="cite_ref-61"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup>
6.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-92 "Jump up")** The term _Euromaidan_; was initially used as a [hashtag](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashtag "Hashtag") on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-What's_in_a_name_89-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-What's_in_a_name-89">[84]</a></sup> A Twitter account named Euromaidan was created on the first day of the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-90"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-90">[85]</a></sup> It soon became popular in the international media.<sup id="cite_ref-91"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-91">[86]</a></sup> It is composed of two parts: _Euro_ is short for Europe and _maidan_ refers to [Maidan Nezalezhnosti](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maidan_Nezalezhnosti "Maidan Nezalezhnosti") (Independence Square), the main square of [Kyiv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyiv "Kyiv"), where the protests were centered.<sup id="cite_ref-What's_in_a_name_89-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-What's_in_a_name-89">[84]</a></sup>
7.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-132 "Jump up")** On 7 April 2013 a decree by [Ukrainian President](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_President "Ukrainian President") [Viktor Yanukovych](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych "Viktor Yanukovych") freed [Yuriy Lutsenko](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuriy_Lutsenko "Yuriy Lutsenko") from prison and exempted him from further punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-Lutpar7413_131-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-Lutpar7413-131">[125]</a></sup>
8.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-149 "Jump up")** On 20 December 2013 Ukrainian Prime Minister [Mykola Azarov](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mykola_Azarov "Mykola Azarov") stated that the public had not been given clear explanations by the authorities of the reason of the decree suspended preparations for signing of the association agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-148">[141]</a></sup>
9.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-155 "Jump up")** On 10 December President Yanukovych stated "We will certainly resume the IMF negotiations. If there are conditions that suit us, we will take that path."<sup id="cite_ref-IMFY101213_154-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-IMFY101213-154">[146]</a></sup> However, Yanukovych also (once again) stated that the conditions put forward by the IMF were unacceptable "I had a conversation with U.S. Vice President Joseph Biden, who told me that the issue of the IMF loan has almost been solved, but I told him that if the conditions remained ... we did not need such loans."<sup id="cite_ref-IMFY101213_154-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-IMFY101213-154">[146]</a></sup>
10.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-313 "Jump up")** According to the _[Financial Times](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Times "Financial Times")_, people in [East Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Ukraine "East Ukraine") and [South Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ukraine "South Ukraine") "tend to be more politically passive than their western counterparts. Locals say they still feel part of Ukraine and have no desire to reunite with Russia – nor are they likely to engage in conflict with the west".<sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_note-312">[303]</a></sup>

116.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euromaidan#cite_ref-123 "Jump up")** Timothy Snyder (20 March 2014). ["Fascism, Russia, and Ukraine"](http://www.nybooks.com/articles/archives/2014/mar/20/fascism-russia-and-ukraine/). _The New York Review of Books_. Retrieved 3 March 2014. But a maidan now means in Ukrainian what the Greek word agora means in English: not just a marketplace where people happen to meet, but a place where they deliberately meet, precisely in order to deliberate, to speak, and to create a political society. During the protests the word maidan has come to mean the act of public politics itself, so that for example people who use their cars to organize public actions and protect other protestors are called the automaidan.
